Witness Requirements for Crescent Sighting: Ramadan and Eid
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness numbers for crescent sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of witnesses required for Ramadan and Eid crescents under cloudy and clear sky conditions, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the issue.

Core Idea
One witness for Ramadan cloudy, two for Eid cloudy, multitude for all when clear.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the nuanced Hanafi position on witnessing the crescent for Ramadan and Eid. While the rule seems straightforward, the school contains significant internal differences on the precise number and even on which crescent follows which rule. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the fiqh of moon sighting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
Distinguish between cloudy (or other atmospheric obstruction) and clear sky conditions. The ruling differs based on weather.
2
Extract the mufta bihi number for each crescent
For Ramadan: one just witness when cloudy, multitude when clear. For Eid al-Fitr and al-Adha: two men or a man and two women when cloudy, multitude when clear.
Note that al-Adha is treated like al-Fitr in the relied-upon position.
3
List the intra-Hanafi opinions on clear sky
Abu Hanifa (one view): accepts one witness for Ramadan even in clear sky. Abu Yusuf requires multitude equal to qasamah (50). Muhammad leaves it to the judge's discretion.
The mufta bihi is the multitude requirement (zahir al-riwayah).
4
Note the exception for witnesses from outside the city or elevated places
A single witness coming from outside the city or in an elevated place within the city is accepted even for clear sky, because certainty is higher.
5
Apply the ruling to the nine other crescents
For all other months, the rule is like Eid: two witnesses required, regardless of weather, unless the witness is from outside the city.
This is per al-Asbijabi and is the relied-upon position.

ذلك الخ. وفيها عن الحجة ولو قبل الإمام شهادة شاهدين عدلين وقد سقط قلب القاضي على قولهما جاز وثبت حكم رمضان . قوله : (قول الطحاوي) خبر قوله «فرق». وفي الذخيرة : إنما لا تقبل شهادة الواحد على هلال رمضان إذا كانت السماء مصحية إذا كان هذا الواحد في المصر، وأما إذا جاء خارج المصر أو جاء من أعلى الأماكن في مصر ذكر الطحاوي رحمه الله أنه تقبل شهادته، وهكذا ذكر في كتاب الاستحسان. وذكر في القدوري أنه لا تقبل Two men or a man and two women for [Eid] al-Fitr, otherwise a great multitude, and al-Adha is like al-Fitr. And there is no consideration of difference in rising places. That is due to an excuse as in the sick and traveler, and fasting Ramadan before Ramadan is not permitted with any excuse, so resorting to what is permitted with an excuse is more appropriate. Then if the testimony of one is not accepted and need for increased number: from Abu Hanifa that the testimony of two men or a man and two women is accepted; from Abu Yusuf that it is not accepted unless they testify upon a great multitude, and that is estimated by the number of qasamah; from Khalaf ibn Ayyub: five hundred in Balkh is few; from Abu Hafs al-Kabir: he stipulated [that it be] sufficient; from Muhammad: whatever the judge deems many is many, and whatever he deems few is few. This is when the one who testified is in the city; but if he came from another place outside the city, his testimony is accepted if he is just and trustworthy because he is certain of the sighting in deserts, not certain in cities due to much dust. Similarly if he is in the city in an elevated place. And the crescent of al-Fitr if the sky is clear is like the crescent of Ramadan. This indicates the preference of the narration of al-Hasan, and that the zahir al-riwayah considers number, not the great multitude, but he distinguished between one who is in the city and outside it, and between the elevated place and otherwise, according to al-Tahawi. As for zahir al-riwayah, the report of a single person is not accepted absolutely, as in Ghayat al-Bayan and Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'and al-Adha is like al-Fitr' meaning the crescent of Dhul Hijjah is like the crescent of Shawwal, so it is not established during clouds except by two men or a man and two women. As for the clear sky condition, all are alike: increase in number is necessary as we have presented. It is only like its crescent and not Ramadan because the right of the servants is attached to it, which is expansion through the meat of sacrifices. It is mentioned in al-Nawadir from Abu Hanifa that it is like Ramadan because a religious matter is attached to it, which is the obligation of sacrifice. The first is the apparent madhhab as in al-Khulasah. It is zahir al-riwayah and it is the most correct as in al-Hidayah and its commentaries and al-Tabyin. The author of al-Tuhfah corrected the second, so there is difference in correction, but the first is supported because it is the madhhab. He did not touch on the ruling of the remaining nine crescents. Imam al-Asbijabi mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi al-Kabir: As for the crescent of al-Fitr and al-Adha and other crescents, only the testimony of two men or a man and two women, just free men not subject to hadd punishment, is accepted as in all other legal matters. This is zahir al-riwayah contrary to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, rather it requires increase in number, and they differed on its amount. In it, from al-Hujja: if the Imam accepts the testimony of two just witnesses and the judge's heart is satisfied with their statement, it is permissible and the ruling of Ramadan is established. His statement: 'the statement of al-Tahawi' is the predicate of his statement 'he distinguished'. In al-Dhakhirah: The testimony of one on the crescent of Ramadan is only not accepted when the sky is clear and this one is in the city. But if he came from outside the city or from an elevated place in the city, al-Tahawi mentioned that his testimony is accepted. Thus it is mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan. It is mentioned in al-Quduri that his testimony is not accepted in zahir al-riwayah, and al-Karkhi mentioned that it is accepted. In al-Aqdiyyah, he corrected the narration of al-Tahawi and relied upon it. His statement: 'only the testimony of two men etc. is accepted.' Al-Ramli said: Apparently in the nine crescents, there is no difference between whether there is a cloud cover in the sky or not regarding acceptance of two men or
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of witnesses required for sighting the crescent of Ramadan, Shawwal (Eid al-Fitr), and Dhul Hijjah (Eid al-Adha). The matn states: 'For al-Fitr, two men or a man and two women; otherwise a great multitude; al-Adha is like al-Fitr.' The commentator expands on the conditions. The core ruling: when the sky is cloudy, only two men or a man and two women are needed for Ramadan? No, the matn says 'for al-Fitr'. The commentary clarifies that for Ramadan under clouds, one just witness suffices in the Hanafi school, but for al-Fitr and al-Adha, two men or a man and two women are required. If the sky is clear, a great multitude (jama' 'azim) is needed for all three, but there is dispute on the exact number. Abu Hanifa holds that even in clear sky, two men or a man and two women are enough; but the zahir al-riwayah requires a multitude. The various opinions: Abu Yusuf requires a multitude equal to the number of qasamah (50). Muhammad says it depends on the judge's discretion. The text then discusses exceptions: if the witness comes from outside the city or is in an elevated place, their testimony is accepted as if the sky were cloudy. For al-Adha, there are two positions: one that it is like al-Fitr (requiring two), and another (in Nawadir from Abu Hanifa) that it is like Ramadan (accepting one just witness under clouds). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first: al-Adha like al-Fitr. The passage ends with a discussion of whether the condition applies to all nine other crescents (i.e., all months besides Ramadan). Some scholars say the rule for two witnesses applies to all crescents; others restrict to these two.

Key Terms
جمع عظيم (jam' 'azim): A large multitude of witnesses sufficient to produce certainty; exact number disputed.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent transmission of the school from Abu Hanifa's disciples (especially Muhammad al-Shaybani) as opposed to rare narrations (nawadir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of witnesses required to establish the crescent of Shawwal (Eid al-Fitr) when the sky is cloudy according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) One just man
B) Two men or a man and two women
C) A great multitude
D) Fifty men

Key Takeaway
The number of witnesses for crescent sighting depends on weather and location: one for Ramadan cloudy, two for Eid cloudy, and multitude for all when clear.

The Hanafi Ruling on Ikhtilaf al-Matali: Difference in Rising Places Does Not Break Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute with tarjih on binding nature of sighting across cities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on ikhtilaf al-matali' and apply it to scenarios where news of crescent sighting reaches another city.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf al-matali' is not considered: sighting in one city binds all others once the news is reliably established.

When the crescent of Ramadan or Shawwal is sighted in one city, does that obligation extend to Muslims in another city, even if the moon's rising time differs? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on ikhtilaf al-matali' (difference in rising places). The passage presents the relied-upon view that the difference is disregarded, along with a second view that considers it. Understanding this ruling helps Muslims know when they are obliged to fast or break their fast based on news from another locality.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the matn declares: 'And there is no consideration of difference in rising places.' This is the starting point for the Hanafi ruling.
2
Identify the opposing view
The text also mentions a second opinion: 'And it is said: it is considered.' This is the other view within the Hanafi school that does consider ikhtilaf al-matali'.
This second view is also attributed to some later Hanafi scholars but is not mufta bihi.
3
Find the tarjih and mufta bihi
The commentator states that the first view is 'zahir al-riwayah, ahwat, and upon it is the fatwa.' This means it is the relied-upon position. Identify the authorities cited (Fath al-Qadir, al-Khulasah).
The term 'zahir al-riwayah' indicates that this position comes from the core Hanafi texts transmitted by Imam Muhammad.
4
Apply the condition: establishment of news
The ruling is not absolute; it requires that the news of sighting be established by a valid means (e.g., testimony before a judge or widespread news that becomes generally known).
The text says 'if it is established before them by a valid means' – this prevents binding by unverified reports.
5
Apply to concrete scenarios
Practice applying the ruling: e.g., the crescent is seen in Damascus; news reaches Baghdad. Under the mufta bihi view, Baghdad must fast. Then contrast with the second view where they would not be bound.
The practical difference (thamarah) is that under the first view, all Muslims in a region must follow the first reliable sighting, while under the second view, each city follows its own sighting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليهم أن قوله : ( ولا عبرة باختلاف المطالع فإذا رآه أهل بلدة ولم يره أهل بلدة أخرى وجب يصوموا برؤية أولئك إذا ثبت عندهم بطريق موجب ويلزم أهل المشرق برؤية أهل المغرب. وقيل يعتبر فلا يلزمهم برؤية غيرهم إذا اختلف المطلع وهو الأشبه. كذا في التبيين، والأول ظاهر الرواية وهو الأحوط . كذا في فتح القدير وظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى كذا في الخلاصة . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بينهما تفاوت بحيث يختلف المطلع أولاً، وقيدنا بالثبوت المذكور لأنه لو شهد جماعة أن أهل بلد كذا رأوا هلال رمضان قبلكم بيوم فصاموا وهذا اليوم لكن قوله : ( ولا عبرة باختلاف المطالع ...
Upon them that his statement: 'And there is no consideration of difference in rising places. So if the people of a town see it and the people of another town do not see it, they must fast upon the sighting of those [first] if it is established before them by a valid means, and the people of the East are bound by the sighting of the people of the West.' And it is said: it is considered, so they are not bound by the sighting of others if the rising place differs, and this is more appropriate. Thus in al-Tabyin, and the first is zahir al-riwayah and it is the most precautionary. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and it is the apparent madhhab and upon it is the fatwa, thus in al-Khulasah. He made it absolute, so it includes whether there is a difference such that the rising place differs or not. And we qualified with the aforementioned establishment because if a group testifies that the people of such a town saw the crescent of Ramadan a day before you and they fasted, and this day...
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on the issue of ikhtilaf al-matali' (difference in lunar rising places). The matn states: 'And there is no consideration of difference in rising places.' The commentary explains the ruling: if people of one town see the crescent (for Ramadan or Eid), then people of another town—even if they did not see it—must fast or break their fast accordingly, provided the news reaches them through a legally valid means (e.g., testimony accepted by a judge). This binds the East to the West's sighting. There is a contrary opinion (qila) that considers the difference in rising places, so people are not bound if the rising place differs. The commentator notes that the first view (no consideration) is zahir al-riwayah, the more precautionary (ahwat), the apparent madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa. The ruling is absolute: it applies whether the distance is large so that the rising times differ or not. However, the commentator qualifies that the news must be established (mustafid) or reliably reported. The text ends mid-sentence with an example about a group testifying that another town saw the moon a day earlier. This part includes a historical application: a case in Damascus where news from Beirut and Homs conflicted, and the discussion of whether widespread news (istifada) binds people. The relied-upon position is that the first news, if established, must be followed, even if other cities differ.

Key Terms
اختلاف المطالع (ikhtilaf al-matali'): Difference in the rising places (time/angle) of the new moon due to geographical distance.
استفاضة الخبر (istifadat al-khabar): Widespread news that reaches the level of general knowledge without formal testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the crescent of Ramadan is sighted in Marrakesh, are Muslims in Cairo required to begin fasting if the news reaches them through a reliable report?
A) Yes, because difference in rising places is not considered
B) No, because the rising place differs between the two cities
C) Only if both cities share the same horizon
D) Only if the sighting is confirmed by a multitude of witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi view is that ikhtilaf al-matali' is not considered: a reliable sighting in one city obligates all others to follow.

The Hanafi Ruling on Ikhtilaf al-Matali'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on moon sighting obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on ikhtilaf al-matali' and distinguish it from the opposing intra-Hanafi and Shafi'i views.

Core Idea
A valid moon sighting obligates all Muslims to fast, regardless of location.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi dispute about whether the sighting of the crescent moon in one locality obligates fasting upon another locality where the moon was not sighted, particularly when the rising places (matali') differ. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two positions within the Hanafi school and clarifies the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. Understanding this ruling is essential for Muslims living in regions that may not sight the moon themselves but have reliable reports from elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
Read the opening lines: 'لا عبرة باختلاف المطالع' and 'وقيل يعتبر'. The first is the position that gives no consideration to differing rising places; the second (qila) does give consideration. Note that the first is described as 'zahir al-riwaya' and 'mufta bihi'.
The author uses technical terms: 'zahir al-riwaya' (the transmitted core) and 'mufta bihi' (the operative view).
2
Analyze the Proof Structure
Examine the evidence for each position. The first relies on the general principle that a proven sighting binds all, supported by the statement that easterners are bound by westerners' sighting. The opposing view (attributed to some Hanafis and Shafi'is) argues that when the rising place differs, each region follows its own sighting.
No explicit textual proof is quoted; the argument is based on the logical implication of unity of the Ummah versus local observation.
3
Understand the Tarjih (Preference)
The author (Ibn Nujaym) cites multiple authorities: al-Tabyin, Fath al-Qadir, al-Khulasa, all affirming the first position as the apparent school and basis of fatwa. The term 'ahwat' (more precautionary) is used, indicating it is safer in practice.
Tarjih is based on the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah and the principle that fasting is an act of worship that should be observed uniformly.
4
Examine the Means of Proof
The passage discusses how a sighting is proven: testimony of two just men or a man and two women when there is no obstruction; if obstruction exists, a large multitude is required. Also, 'istifada' (widespread report) is a valid proof if verified.
These conditions affect whether the sighting is considered 'thābit' (established) and thus binding on others.
5
Apply a Historical Example
The author recounts an incident in Damascus (1239 AH) where conflicting widespread reports emerged. The analysis shows how the principle of binding by proven sighting is applied in practice, even when there is apparent contradiction.
This step demonstrates the real-world application of the legal theory.

المطلع وهو الأشبه. كذا في التبيين، والأول ظاهر الرواية وهو الأحوط . كذا في فتح القدير وظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى كذا في الخلاصة . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بينهما تفاوت بحيث يختلف المطلع أولاً، وقيدنا بالثبوت المذكور لأنه لو شهد جماعة أن أهل بلد كذا رأوا هلال رمضان قبلكم بيوم فصاموا وهذا اليوم لكن الرجل والمرأتين لفقد العلة الموجبة لاشتراط الجمع الكثير وهي توجه الكل طالبين، ويؤيده قوله كما في سائر الأحكام، فلو شهد رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان بهلال شعبان ولم يكن بالسماء علة يثبت، وإذا ثبت يثبت رمضان بعد ثلاثين يوماً من يوم ثبوته كما هو ظاهر، لكن بعد اجتماع شرائط الثبوت الشرعي. فإن قلت : فيه إثبات ويوافقة إطلاق عبارة مواهب الرحمن حيث قال: وأثبتوه بقول عدل إن اعتل المطلع وشرط للفطر حران أو حر وحرتان، والأضحى كالفطر في ظاهر الرواية، وإن لم يعتل فجمع عظيم للكل والاكتفاء بالاثنين رواية ا هـ . لكن قوله «للكل» يحتمل كل الأشهر، ويحتمل كل الثلاثة المذكورة في كلامه وهو أقرب لأنه لم يتعرض لغيرها وصاحب الإمداد شديد المتابعة لصاحب المواهب فإن كان مستنده ذلك ففيه نظر لما علمت من احتمال العبارة والله صاموا الخميس لكن استفاض الخبر عن عامة البلاد سوى هذين البلدين أنهم صاموا الجمعة مثل دمشق، فهل تعتبر الاستفاضة الأولى في مخالفتها للثانية أو لا بناء على أن الظاهر يعتقضي غلط أهل تلك البلدتين نظير ما مر فيما لو كانت السماء مصحية ورأى الهلال واحد لا يعتبر لأن التفرد من بين الجم الغفير ظاهر في ا الغلط مع أنه ليس بين تلك البلاد بعد كثير بحيث تختلف به المطالع، لكن ظاهر الإطلاق يقتضي لزوم عامة البلاد ما ثبت عنه بلدة أخرى، فكل من استفاض عندهم خبر تلك البلدة يلزمهم اتباع أهلها، ويدل عليه قوله : ويلزم أهل المشرق برؤية أهل المغرب إذ ليس المراد بأهل المشرق جميعهم بل بلدة واحدة تكفي كما لا يخفى. وإذا كان هذا تختلف فيها مع بعد المسافة التي . ثم اعلم أن المراد بالاستفاضة تواتر الخبر من الواردين من بلدة الثبوت إلى البلدة التي لم يثبت بها لا مجرد الاستفاضة لأنها قد تكون مبنية على إخبار رجل واحد مثلاً فيشيع الخبر عنه، ولا شك أن هذا لا يكفي بدليل قولهم إذا استفاض الخبر وتحقق فإن التحقق لا يكون إلا بما ذكرنا . تتمة : لم يذكروا عندنا العمل بالأمارات الظاهرة الدالة على ثبوت الشهر كضرب المدافع في زماننا، والظاهر وجوب العمل بها على من سمعها ممن كان غائباً عن المصر كأهل القرى ونحوها كما يجب العمل بها على أهل المصر الذين لم يروا الحاكم قبل شهادة الشهود، وقد ذكر هذا الفرع الشافعية فصرح ابن حجر في التحفة أنه يثبت بالأمارة الظاهرة الدالة التي لا تتخلف عادة كرؤية القناديل المعلقة بالمنائر قال : ومخالفة جمع في ذلك غير صحيحة ا هـ .
His saying: (And no consideration is given to the difference of rising places. So when the people of a town see it [the crescent] and the people of another town do not see it, they must fast by their sighting if it is proven to them by a binding method. And the people of the east are bound by the sighting of the people of the west. And it is said: consideration is given, so they are not bound by the sighting of others when the rising place differs, and this is more appropriate. Thus in al-Tabyin, and the first is the apparent narration and it is more precautionary. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, and it is the apparent school and upon it is the fatwa, thus in al-Khulasa. He made it absolute so it includes both when there is a distance such that the rising place differs and when not. And we qualified it by the mentioned proof because if a group testifies that the people of such a town saw the crescent of Ramadan a day before you and fasted, and this day... but a man and two women due to the lack of the cause necessitating a large assembly, which is the direction of all seekers. And it is supported by his saying as in all other rulings. So if two men or a man and two women testify to the crescent of Sha'ban and there is no obstruction in the sky, it is proven. And when it is proven, Ramadan is proven after thirty days from its day of proof as is apparent, but after the conditions of legal proof are met. If you say: This proves Ramadan without the cause by the report of two men or a man and two women, and we negated it. I say: Its proof in this case is incidental, and what is overlooked in incidental matters is not overlooked in intended matters. Reflect on it. It is explicitly stated in al-Imdad contrary to this, so he required a large assembly when there is no obstruction, and the absolute wording of Mawahib al-Rahman agrees with him where he said: And they prove it by the word of a just person if the rising place is obstructed, and he stipulated for breaking the fast two free men or a free man and two free women, and the sacrifice is like the breaking of the fast in the apparent narration. And if it is not obstructed, then a large assembly for all, and sufficiency with two is a narration. But his word 'for all' could mean all months or all three mentioned in his speech, and the latter is more likely because he did not address others. And the author of al-Imdad is very following of the author of al-Mawahib; if his reliance is that, it is questionable as you know from the probability of the wording. And Allah knows best. His saying: (And we qualified it by the mentioned proof) etc. He said in al-Sharnabaliyya: And in al-Mughni, Imam al-Halwani said: The correct in our school is that when a report becomes widespread in another town and is verified, they are bound by the ruling of that town. And it is attributed in al-Durr al-Mukhtar to al-Mujtaba and others. And similar in al-Dhakhira with the text: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The correct in our school is that when a report becomes widespread and verified among the people of the other town, they are bound by the ruling of this town. I say: This incident occurred in Damascus in the year 1239 AH. Ramadan was proven in Damascus on Friday night after thirty days of Sha'ban, and there was an obstruction in the sky that night. Then the report became widespread from the people of Beirut and Homs that they fasted on Thursday. But the report became widespread from all other cities besides these two that they fasted on Friday like Damascus. So is the first widespread report considered in its contradiction to the second or not, based on the apparent presumption that the people of those two towns were mistaken, similar to what passed regarding if the sky is clear and one person sees the crescent, it is not considered because one individual among the large multitude is clearly mistaken, especially since there is not much distance between those towns such that the rising places differ. But the apparent absolute wording necessitates that all towns are bound by what is proven from another town. So whoever hears a widespread report of that town is bound to follow its people. And it is indicated by his saying: And the people of the east are bound by the sighting of the people of the west, because the intended meaning of 'people of the east' is not all of them but one town is sufficient, as is not hidden. And if this differs in it with distance... Then know that what is meant by widespread report is the continuous report from those coming from the town of proof to the town that has not proven it, not mere widespread report because it may be based on the report of one man, for example, and then the report spreads from him. There is no doubt that this is insufficient, as indicated by their saying: when the report becomes widespread and verified, verification only occurs as we mentioned. Addendum: They did not mention in our school acting on apparent signs indicating the proof of the month, like firing cannons in our time. It is apparent that acting on them is obligatory for those who hear them who are absent from the city, like villagers and the like, just as it is obligatory for the people of the city who have not seen the judge before the testimony of witnesses. And this branch has been mentioned by the Shafi'is: Ibn Hajar stated in al-Tuhfa that it is proven by the apparent sign that does not usually fail, like seeing lamps hung on minarets. He said: And opposition to this by a group is not correct.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the sighting of the crescent moon in one locality obligates fasting upon another locality where the moon was not sighted, given differing rising places (matali'). The author presents two positions. The first, which is 'zahir al-riwaya' and the basis of fatwa, states that there is no consideration for differing rising places: if the sighting is legally proven (e.g., by two just witnesses or widespread report), all Muslims must fast regardless of distance. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. The second position, called 'al-ashbah' by some, gives consideration to differing rising places so that one locality is not bound by another. However, the author affirms the first opinion as 'ahwat' (more precautionary). He then discusses the mode of proof: testimony of two men or a man and two women is sufficient when there is no obstruction (cause) in the sky; when there is obstruction, a large multitude is required. He also discusses 'istifada' (widespread report) as a valid proof, citing Imam al-Halwani that widespread and verified news binds the other town. The author relates a historical case from Damascus in 1239 AH and discusses the conflict of widespread reports. He also touches on modern practice of using cannons as indicators, stating it is obligatory to act on them, and cites Shafi'i support.

Key Terms
اختلاف المطالع (ikhtilāf al-maṭāliʿ): The difference in the rising places of the moon (i.e., different longitudes) that can cause one region to see the crescent before another.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The ruling transmitted in the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah), which is the standard authority in the Hanafi school.
الاستفاضة (al-istifāḍah): Widespread report or continuous narration from multiple sources that leads to certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ikhtilaf al-matali'?
A) Consideration is given to differing rising places, so each locality follows its own sighting.
B) No consideration is given; a proven sighting obligates all Muslims regardless of location.
C) Only two just witnesses can obligate fasting in another locality.
D) The sighting must come from a large multitude to be binding.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a legally proven moon sighting from any locality obligates all Muslims to fast, regardless of differing rising places.

The Hanafi Definition: Fasad and Batal Are Synonymous in Ibadat
Definition of fasad/batal in ibadat as synonymous

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view that fasad and batalan are synonymous in acts of worship (ibadat) and distinguish this from their usage in transactions (muamalat).

Core Idea
In ibadat, fasad and batal are the same: the act is invalid and must be repeated.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on invalidators of fasting but quickly establishes a key definitional principle: in acts of worship, the terms 'fasid' and 'batil' are synonymous. This is different from transactions, where Hanafi jurists distinguish between a defective contract (fasid) and a void one (batil). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying rulings on fasting and other acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Ruling Context
The text is defining terms within the chapter on fasting. Note that it addresses the meanings of 'sihha', 'fasad', and 'batalan' in ibadat.
These terms appear in the context of fasting but apply to all ibadat.
2
2. Extract the Definition
The text states: 'الصحة، الفساد والبطلان في العبادات بمعنى واحد'. This means soundness, corruption, and invalidity are synonymous in ibadat. They all refer to the legal consequence of the act.
3
3. Understand the Consequence
The consequence of an act being fasid or batil in ibadat is that it is invalid and must be made up (qada). The text says 'اندفاع القضاء بالإتيان بالشرائط والأركان' - meaning soundness repels the obligation of qada when conditions and pillars are fulfilled, so fasad/batal mean the opposite: qada is required.
Even though the phrasing is about soundness, the logical inverse gives the definition of fasad/batal.
4
4. Contrast with Transactions
The text explicitly contrasts ibadat with muamalat: 'بخلافهما في المعاملات'. In transactions, fasad and batal are not synonymous; a fasid contract can be rectified, while a batil one is void from the start.
This is a unique Hanafi position. Shafi'is treat them as synonymous in both domains.

Source Text

For if the fasting person eats or drinks or has intercourse forgetfully, or has a wet dream, or emits semen by looking, or applies oil, or... thirty according to their calculation and they did not see the crescent. Commentary
This passage is a fragmentary opening of the chapter 'What invalidates the fast and what does not'. The OCR is corrupted, mixing parts of the previous discussion on moon sighting with the chapter's content. The core legal point that emerges is a definition: In acts of worship (ibadat), the terms 'fasad' (corruption) and 'batalan' (invalidity) are synonymous—both mean that the act is not valid and must be repeated (qada). This is distinguished from transactions (muamalat), where 'fasad' and 'batal' may differ: a fasid transaction is one that can be rectified, while a batil one is void from the start. The author then notes that this distinction is a rational judgment, not a positive legal ruling. The passage also includes a list of invalidators (eating, drinking, intercourse forgetfully, etc.), but the OCR cuts off mid-list. The remainder of the OCR text appears to be a continuation of the earlier discussion on moon sighting, not part of the chapter. Thus, this lesson only covers the definitional ruling.

Key Terms
الفساد (al-fasād): In ibadat: same as batalan, meaning the act is invalid and must be made up (qada). In transactions: a separate category where the contract is defective but can be rectified.
البطلان (al-buṭlān): Invalidity; in ibadat synonymous with fasad; in transactions, a contract that is void ab initio.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the relationship between fasad and batalan in acts of worship (ibadat)?
A) They are distinct: fasad is less severe than batalan.
B) They are synonymous: both mean the act is invalid and requires qada.
C) Fasad applies to transactions only, not ibadat.
D) Batalan is for minor defects, fasad for major ones.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, fasad and batalan are synonymous in ibadat, both meaning the act is invalid and requires qada; this differs from transactions where they are distinct.

Forgetful Eating Does Not Invalidate the Fast: The Hadith Proof
Proof from hadith that forgetful acts do not break the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful eating while fasting and explain the hadith proof used.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness in fasting is an excuse; the fast remains valid and no qada is required.

We begin with a well-known hadith that establishes a key principle in the fiqh of fasting: forgetful acts do not break the fast. The Hanafi school relies on this text to rule that the fast is valid, and no compensation is needed. However, there are nuances regarding reminders and compelling reasons that we will explore later. First, let us examine the primary proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating or drinking forgetfully while fasting. The ruling from the hadith is that the fast is valid and must be completed.
The hadith explicitly says 'let him complete his fast'.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks, let him complete his fast, for Allah fed him and gave him drink.' Narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning and qat'i al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyutim' indicates the fast remains valid; the phrase 'Allah fed him' shows the act is not attributed to the servant, thus no sin or invalidity.
The phrase 'Allah fed him' removes the act from the servant's responsibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Most schools agree that forgetful eating does not invalidate, but Hanafi explicitly says no qada or kaffarah is required. Other schools may require qada.
The passage cites Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'No qada is due upon you'.
5
Apply to other acts
Intercourse is included by implication (dalala) because it is a pillar of fasting, not by analogy, thus refuting those who would analogize it as invalidating.
The analogy would break the fast, but the hadith's implication prevents it.

Source Text

قوله (فإن أكل الصائم أو شرب أو جامع ناسياً إلى آخره الحديث الجماعة إلا النسائي من نسي وهو صائم فأكل أو شرب فليتم صومه فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الصو باب ٢٦ مسلم في كتاب الصيام حديث ۱۷. ابن ماجه في " الصيام باب ١٥ الدامي في كتاب الصوم باب ۲۳ أحمد في مسنده (٢/ ٣٩٥، ٤٢٥). والمراد بالصوم الشرعي لا اللغوي الذي هو مطلق الإمساك للاتفاق على أن الحمل على المفهوم الشرعي حيث أمكن في لفظ الشارع واجب خصوصاً قد ورد في صحيح ابن حبان «ولا قضاء عليك» وعند البزار «فلا يفطر». وألحق الجماع به دلالة للاستواء في الركنية لا قياساً فاندفع به القياس المقتضي للفطر لفوات الركن. وحقيقة النسيان عدم استحضار الشيء وقت حاجته قالوا: وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوقه تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم فإن كان مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي لم يسقط لتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة فإنه ساقط لوجود الداعي، وإن لم مع مذكر وله داع كأكل الصائم سقط، وإن لم يكن معه مذكور ولا داع فأولى بالسقوط كترك الذابح التسمية. وخرج ما إذا أكل ناسياً فذكره إنسان بالصوم ولم يتذذكر فأكل فسد صومه في الصحيح خلافاً لبعضهم - كذا في الظهيرية - لأنه أخبر بأن هذا الأكل حرام عليه، وخبر الواحد في الديانات مقبول فكان يجب أن يلتفت إلى تأمل الحال لوجود المذكر. والأولى أن لا يذكره إن كان شيخاً لأن ما يفعله الصائم ليس بمعصية فالسكوت عنه ليس
His saying: 'If the fasting person eats or drinks or has intercourse forgetfully' to the end of the hadith. The group except al-Nasa'i: 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks, let him complete his fast, for Allah fed him and gave him drink.' (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari in the Book of Fasting, Chapter 26; Muslim in the Book of Fasting, Hadith 17; Ibn Majah in 'Fasting', Chapter 15; al-Darimi in the Book of Fasting, Chapter 23; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/395, 425). And what is meant is the legal fast, not the linguistic meaning which is mere abstention, because it is unanimously agreed that applying the legal meaning to the words of the Lawgiver is obligatory when possible, especially since it is narrated in Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'No qada is due upon you' and by al-Bazzar: 'He does not break fast'. And intercourse is attached to it by implication due to equality in being a pillar, not by analogy, thus repelling the analogy that would require breaking the fast due to loss of the pillar. The reality of forgetfulness is non‑recollection of a thing at the time of need. They said: It is not an excuse in the rights of people, but in the rights of Allah it is an excuse for the removal of sin. As for the ruling: if there is a reminder and no compelling reason (like the prayer who eats forgetfully), it does not [cause the act to be] invalidated due to his negligence, unlike his salam during the sitting because it is invalidated due to the existence of compulsion. If there is a reminder and a compelling reason (like the fasting person eating forgetfully), it is invalidated. If there is no reminder and no compelling reason, it is even more likely to be invalidated, like the slaughterer leaving the tasmiyah. And there is the case where one eats forgetfully, then a person reminds him of the fast but he does not recall and eats; his fast becomes invalid in the correct view, contrary to some, as in al-Zahiriyyah, because he was informed that this eating is forbidden upon him, and the report of a single person in religious matters is acceptable, so he should have reflected upon the situation due to the existence of a reminder. And it is better not to remind him if he is an elderly person, because what the fasting person does is not a sin, so remaining silent about it is not...
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof from the hadith that if a fasting person forgetfully eats, drinks, or has intercourse, their fast remains valid and no qada or kaffarah is required. The commentator explains that the hadith applies to the sharʿī fast, not merely linguistic abstention. Intercourse is included by implication (dalāla) because it is a pillar of fasting, not by analogy, thus refuting those who would analogize it to invalidating acts. The text then defines forgetfulness (nisyān) as the absence of recollection at the time of need. It explains that forgetfulness is an excuse in the rights of Allah (removing sin) but not in the rights of people. The ruling on validity depends on whether there is a reminder (mudhakkir) and a compelling reason (dāʿī). If there is no reminder and no compelling reason, the act is invalidated (e.g., leaving tasmiyah in slaughter). If there is a reminder but no compelling reason, the act is not invalidated due to negligence. The example of the fasting person: if he eats forgetfully and then is reminded but still eats, his fast becomes invalid because the reminder makes him aware of the prohibition. However, it is better not to remind an elderly person if reminding might cause hardship, as the forgetful act itself is not a sin.

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyān): The absence of recollection of something at the time of need.
الدلالة (al-dalāla): Implication; inferring a ruling from a text through contextual or semantic connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what should a fasting person do if they forgetfully eat?
A) Break the fast and make it up later.
B) Complete the fast because it is still valid.
C) Continue fasting but pay kaffarah.
D) Stop eating immediately and then make up the fast.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful eating or drinking while fasting does not invalidate the fast, and no qada is required, based on the explicit hadith.

Effect of Reminders and Compelling Reasons on Forgetful Acts in Fasting
Expansion on the factors affecting the ruling on forgetful acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a forgetful act invalidates the fast according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A reminder or absence of a compelling reason removes the excuse of forgetfulness.

While the basic ruling is that forgetful acts do not break the fast, the Hanafi school adds a crucial nuance: if a person was reminded of the fast or had no compelling reason to act, the excuse of forgetfulness is removed. This lesson unpacks the terms mudhakkir (reminder) and dāʿī (compelling reason) and how they affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define forgetfulness (nisyān)
Nisyān is the absence of recollection at the time of need. It is an excuse in the rights of Allah but not in the rights of people.
This definition sets the scope of the excuse.
2
Distinguish between rights of Allah and rights of people
Forgetfulness removes sin in Allah's rights (e.g., fasting) but not in people's rights (e.g., property).
This explains why the fast is not sinful but may still be invalid if negligence is present.
3
Identify the two factors: mudhakkir and dāʿī
Mudhakkir is a reminder; dāʿī is a compelling reason that drives the act (e.g., hunger).
These factors determine whether the forgetfulness is excusable.
4
Apply the factors to scenarios
If there is a reminder but no compelling reason (e.g., eating during prayer), the act is not excused. If there is a reminder and a compelling reason (fasting person reminded but still eats), the fast becomes invalid. Without either, it is even more clearly invalid.
The fasting person scenario is the focus: reminder removes the excuse.
5
Examine the specific case of the fasting person
The correct view (as in al-Ẓahīriyyah) is that if a fasting person is reminded and still eats, the fast becomes invalid. However, it is better not to remind an elderly person because the act is not a sin.
This shows consideration for the person's situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فإن أكل الصائم أو شرب أو جامع ناسياً إلى آخره الحديث الجماعة إلا النسائي من نسي وهو صائم فأكل أو شرب فليتم صومه فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الصو باب ٢٦ مسلم في كتاب الصيام حديث ۱۷. ابن ماجه في " الصيام باب ١٥ الدامي في كتاب الصوم باب ۲۳ أحمد في مسنده (٢/ ٣٩٥، ٤٢٥). والمراد بالصوم الشرعي لا اللغوي الذي هو مطلق الإمساك للاتفاق على أن الحمل على المفهوم الشرعي حيث أمكن في لفظ الشارع واجب خصوصاً قد ورد في صحيح ابن حبان «ولا قضاء عليك» وعند البزار «فلا يفطر». وألحق الجماع به دلالة للاستواء في الركنية لا قياساً فاندفع به القياس المقتضي للفطر لفوات الركن. وحقيقة النسيان عدم استحضار الشيء وقت حاجته قالوا: وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوقه تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم فإن كان مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي لم يسقط لتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة فإنه ساقط لوجود الداعي، وإن لم مع مذكر وله داع كأكل الصائم سقط، وإن لم يكن معه مذكور ولا داع فأولى بالسقوط كترك الذابح التسمية. وخرج ما إذا أكل ناسياً فذكره إنسان بالصوم ولم يتذذكر فأكل فسد صومه في الصحيح خلافاً لبعضهم - كذا في الظهيرية - لأنه أخبر بأن هذا الأكل حرام عليه، وخبر الواحد في الديانات مقبول فكان يجب أن يلتفت إلى تأمل الحال لوجود المذكر. والأولى أن لا يذكره إن كان شيخاً لأن ما يفعله الصائم ليس بمعصية فالسكوت عنه ليس

Key Terms
المذكر (al-mudhakkir): A reminder or someone who reminds the person of the ruling.
الداعي (al-dāʿī): A compelling reason that drives the act, such as hunger in the case of the fasting person.
حقوق الله (ḥuqūq Allāh): Rights owed to Allah, primarily acts of worship.

D) The fast becomes invalid and requires kaffarah.

Key Takeaway

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Forgetful Acts During Fasting: Rulings and Evidence
Sharh on rulings for forgetful acts during fasting with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful eating/drinking/intercourse during fasting, cite the primary hadith evidence, and distinguish the effect of a reminder on the validity of the fast.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not break the fast – Allah fed him; but a reminder can make the fast invalid if ignored.

This lesson examines the well-known hadith that a fasting person who forgetfully eats or drinks must complete his fast, as it was Allah who provided the sustenance. We will unpack the implications, including when a reminder is given, the distinction between linguistic and legal fasting, and how intercourse is treated similarly. Understanding these nuances prevents common misconceptions about fasting and forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary hadith and its significance
The hadith 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks, let him complete his fast, for it is Allah who fed him and gave him drink' is the central proof. Note its narrators and wording. The imperative 'falyutimma' indicates validity and completion.
This hadith is narrated by the group except al-Nasa'i, and also in Sahih Ibn Hibban and al-Bazzar with additional wording negating qada and nullification.
2
Define 'fast' in the legal context
The Prophet's words must be interpreted in the shar'i sense (intentional abstention with intention), not linguistic (mere abstention). This is agreed upon and prevents misinterpretation.
Intercourse is included by indication (dalālah) due to equality in essential nature, not by analogy, thus refuting objections.
3
Analyze the role of forgetfulness and reminder
Forgetfulness (nisyān) is absence of recall at the time of need. It excuses sin in rights of Allah but not in human rights. The presence of a reminder (mudhakkir) and motive (dā'i) affect the ruling: if there is a reminder without motive, the act is not excused; if there is motive without reminder, it is excused.
The analogy of a praying person: eating forgetfully with a reminder invalidates the prayer due to negligence; giving salutation forgetfully in the sitting position is excused due to the motive.
4
Apply the ruling to specific cases
Case 1: Forgetful eating without reminder – fast valid, no qada. Case 2: Forgetful eating with reminder but does not remember – fast invalid in the correct view. Case 3: Forgetful intercourse – if withdraws immediately, valid; if continues and ejaculates, qada but no kaffara unless he moves after remembering.
Ethics of reminding: Better not to remind an old person; for a young person, it is disliked not to remind, and the apparent view is prohibitively disliked.
5
Contrast with mistake and coercion
Mistake (e.g., eating thinking it is not Ramadan) and coercion require qada, unlike forgetfulness. The Shafi'i view treats them like forgetfulness, but Hanafi argues forgetfulness is predominant and from the self, while mistake/coercion are rare and external.
Hadith 'My community is excused for error' is interpreted as otherworldly, not worldly rulings like invalidation of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فإن أكل الصائم أو شرب أو جامع ناسياً إلى آخره الحديث الجماعة إلا النسائي من نسي وهو صائم فأكل أو شرب فليتم صومه فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه (۱) والمراد بالصوم الشرعي لا اللغوي الذي هو مطلق الإمساك للاتفاق على أن الحمل على المفهوم الشرعي حيث أمكن في لفظ الشارع واجب خصوصاً قد ورد في صحيح ابن حبان «ولا قضاء عليك» وعند البزار «فلا يفطر». وألحق الجماع به دلالة للاستواء في الركنية لا قياساً فاندفع به القياس المقتضي للفطر لفوات الركن. وحقيقة النسيان عدم استحضار الشيء وقت حاجته قالوا: وليس عذراً في حقوق العباد وفي حقوقه تعالى عذر في سقوط الإثم، أما الحكم فإن كان مع مذكر ولا داعي إليه كأكل المصلي لم يسقط لتقصيره بخلاف سلامه في القعدة فإنه ساقط لوجود الداعي، وإن لم مع مذكر وله داع كأكل الصائم سقط، وإن لم يكن معه مذكور ولا داع فأولى بالسقوط كترك الذابح التسمية. وخرج ما إذا أكل ناسياً فذكره إنسان بالصوم ولم يتذذكر فأكل فسد صومه في الصحيح خلافاً لبعضهم - كذا في الظهيرية - لأنه أخبر بأن هذا الأكل حرام عليه، وخبر الواحد في الديانات مقبول فكان يجب أن يلتفت إلى تأمل الحال لوجود المذكر. والأولى أن لا يذكره إن كان شيخاً لأن ما يفعله الصائم ليس بمعصية فالسكوت عنه ليس بمعصية، ولأن الشيخوخة مظنة المرحمة. وإن كان شاباً يقوى على الصوم يكره أن لا يخبره، والظاهر أنها تحريمية لأن الولوالجي قال : يلزمه أن يخبره ويكره تركه . أطلقه فشمل الفرض والنفل ولو بدأ بالجماع ناسياً فتذكر أن نزع من ساعته لم يفطر، وإن دام على ذلك أنزل فعليه القضاء ثم قيل لا كفارة عليه وقيل هذا إذا لم يحرك نفسه بعد التذكر حتى أنزل فإن حرك نفسه بعده فعليه الكفارة كما لو نزع ثم أدخل ولو جامع عامداً قبل الفجر وطلع وجب النزع في الحال فإن حرك نفسه فهو على هذا نظير ما قالوا لو أولج ثم قال لها إن جامعتك فأنت طالق أو حرة إن نزع أو لم ينزع ولم يتحرك حتى أنزل لم تطلق ولا تعتق، وإن حرك نفسه طلقت وعتقت ويصير مراجعاً بالحركة الثانية ويجب للأمة العقر ولأحد عليهما. كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : رجل أصبح يوم الشك متلوماً ثم أكل ناسياً ثم ظهر أنه من رمضان ونوى صوماً ذكر في الفتاوى أنه لا يجوز. وفي البقالي : النسيان قبل النية كما بعدها وصححه في القنية . قيد بالناسي لأنه لو كان مخطئاً أو مكرهاً فعليه القضاء خلافاً للشافعي فإنه يعتبر بالناسي ولنا أنه لا يغلب وجوده وعذر النسيان غالب، ولأن النسيان من قبل من له الحق والإكراه من قبل غيره فيفترقان كالمقيد والمريض العاجز عن بالرأس في قضاء الصلاة حيث يقضي المقيد لا المريض. وأما حديث «رفع عن أمتي الخطأ» فهو من باب الاقتضاء وقد أريد الحكم الأخروي فلا حاجة إلى إرادة الدنيوي إذ لا هو
His statement: (If a fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse forgetfully...) to the end of the hadith: the group except al-Nasa'i from the hadith: 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks, let him complete his fast, for it is Allah who fed him and gave him drink.' (1) What is meant is the legal fast, not the linguistic one which is absolute abstention, due to agreement that it is obligatory to interpret the Prophet's words legally when possible, especially since it is reported in Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'There is no qada upon you,' and according to al-Bazzar: 'He does not break his fast.' Intercourse was included by indication due to equality in essential nature, not by analogy; thus the analogy that would necessitate breaking the fast due to loss of the essential element is refuted. The reality of forgetfulness is the absence of recalling something at the time of need. They said: It is not an excuse in the rights of people, but in the rights of Allah it is an excuse for the dropping of sin. As for the ruling: if there is a reminder and no motive (like a praying person eating), it is not dropped due to his negligence, unlike his salutation (salam) in the sitting position which is dropped due to the motive. If there is no reminder and there is a motive (like a fasting person eating), it is dropped. If there is neither a reminder nor a motive, then it is even more deserving of being dropped, like the slaughterer omitting the basmalah. And excluded from this is the case where he eats forgetfully and a person reminds him of the fast but he does not remember, then his fast becomes invalid in the sound opinion, contrary to some – as in al-Zahiriyya – because he is informed that this eating is haram for him, and the report of a single individual in religious matters is accepted, so he must consider the situation due to the existence of a reminder. It is better not to remind him if he is an old man, because what the fasting person does is not a sin, so remaining silent about it is not a sin, and because old age is a place of mercy. If he is a young man capable of fasting, it is disliked not to inform him, and the apparent view is that it is prohibitively disliked, because al-Walwaji said: He must inform him and leaving it is disliked. This is general and includes obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl) fasts. If he begins intercourse forgetfully, then remembers and withdraws immediately, he does not break his fast. If he continues and then has an ejaculation, qada is upon him. Then it is said: There is no kaffara upon him. It is also said: This is if he does not move himself after remembering until he ejaculates. But if he moves himself after remembering, then kaffara is upon him, just as if he withdrew and then inserted. If he has intercourse deliberately before dawn and dawn arrives, he must withdraw immediately. If he moves himself, then it is analogous to what they said: If he inserts and then says to her, 'If I have intercourse with you, you are divorced or free,' if he withdraws or does not withdraw but does not move until he ejaculates, she is not divorced nor freed. But if he moves himself, she is divorced and freed, and he becomes a revocable divorcer by the second movement, and the slave-girl is owed 'uqr' (compensation) and one of them is owed... As in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: A man who woke up on the day of doubt with uncertainty (mutalammim), then ate forgetfully, then it became clear that it was Ramadan, and he intended a fast – it is mentioned in al-Fatawa that it is not permissible. In al-Baqqali: Forgetfulness before the intention is like after it, and he corrected it in al-Qunyah. He restricted it to the forgetful person, because if he was mistaken or coerced, qada is upon him, contrary to al-Shafi'i who treats it like the forgetful person. Our argument: it (mistake/coercion) is not predominant, and the excuse of forgetfulness is predominant; and because forgetfulness is from the one who has the right, while coercion is from someone else, so they differ like the bound person and the sick person who is unable to use his head in making up prayers – the bound person makes up but not the sick. As for the hadith 'My community is excused for error,' it is from the category of implication (iqtida') and what is intended is the otherworldly ruling, so there is no need to intend the worldly ruling, because it is not...
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) by the author on the ruling of a fasting person who forgetfully eats, drinks, or has intercourse. The base text (matn) states that such acts do not break the fast. The author first cites the well-known hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that whoever forgetfully eats or drinks should complete his fast, as Allah provided the sustenance. He clarifies that the term 'fast' here means the legal (shar'i) fast, not mere linguistic abstention, because when possible, the Prophet's words must be interpreted in their legal sense. Evidence from Sahih Ibn Hibban and al-Bazzar confirms that no qada (make-up) is required and the fast is not broken. The author then notes that intercourse is made analogous by indication due to the essential nature of the act, not by analogy (qiyas), thus countering any objection based on analogy that would require breaking the fast. Then the author defines forgetfulness (nisyan) as the absence of recalling something at the time of need. He explains that forgetfulness is not an excuse in human rights but is an excuse in the rights of Allah for dropping sin. However, the ruling on whether the act affects the validity of worship depends on the presence of a reminder (mudhakkir) and a motive (da'i). For example, if a praying person eats forgetfully with a reminder, the prayer is invalid due to negligence; if he gives salutation forgetfully in the sitting posture, it is excused because the motive exists. For a fasting person, if there is a reminder but no motive, the fast is invalid; if there is a motive, it is not invalid. Then the author discusses a specific case: if a forgetful person is reminded by someone else but does not remember, his fast is invalid in the correct view, because the one witness report in religious matters is accepted and he should have considered the situation. Regarding reminding the forgetful person, the author says it is better not to remind an old person because silence is not a sin and old age warrants mercy; for a young man capable of fasting, it is disliked (makruh) not to inform him, and the apparent view is that it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), citing al-Walwaji. This applies to both obligatory and voluntary fasts. Then the author deals with forgetful intercourse: if he remembers and withdraws immediately, no problem; if he continues and ejaculates, qada is required but no kaffara in one opinion; if he moves himself after remembering, kaffara is required. A further case is deliberate intercourse before dawn: if dawn arrives, he must withdraw immediately; any movement after that is analogous to the example of a man saying to his wife conditional divorce. The author then cites al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya on the day of doubt: if a person began the day uncertain (mutalammim), ate forgetfully, then it became clear it was Ramadan, and he intended a fast, it is not permissible (i.e., his fast is not valid). But in al-Baqqali, forgetfulness before intention is like after it, meaning it does not harm. The author concludes by distinguishing between the forgetful and the mistaken or coerced: for the latter, qada is required, unlike al-Shafi'i's view. The reasoning is that mistake and coercion are not predominant, and forgetfulness is a common excuse; additionally, forgetfulness is from the person himself, while coercion is external, analogous to the bound man versus the sick man in making up prayers. Finally, the hadith 'my community is excused for error' is about otherworldly rulings, not worldly ones like invalidation of acts.

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyān): Absence of recalling something at the time of need; an excuse in the rights of Allah for dropping sin, but not in human rights.
المذكّر (al-mudhakkir): A person who reminds the forgetful individual of the legal ruling (e.g., that he is fasting).
الصوم الشرعي (al-ṣawm al-sharʿī): The specific fast as defined by Islamic law: abstention from food, drink, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset with intention.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): Making up a missed or invalidated obligatory act of worship (e.g., fasting) after its time.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): A compensatory expiation for certain violations, e.g., breaking a fast deliberately with intercourse, which requires freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fasting person is reminded that he is fasting while forgetfully eating, and he continues eating, what is the ruling according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) His fast remains valid, no qada required.
B) His fast becomes invalid, and he must make it up (qada).
C) He must continue eating because forgetfulness is an excuse.
D) He must stop and perform kaffara.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful eating/drinking/intercourse does not break the fast, but if a reminder is given and ignored, the fast becomes invalid.

Ruling on Informing a Weak Person about Fasting
States ruling on informing a weak person about fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on informing a person about fasting, distinguishing between an elderly weak person and a young able person, and identify the legal reasoning (talil).

Core Idea
Not informing an elderly weak person is not sinful; not informing a young able person is makruh tahrimi.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on whether one must inform a person about a fast if they may be harmed. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq distinguishes between an elderly weak person, where old age itself invokes mercy, and a young able person, where omitting the information is prohibitively disliked. The ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory fasts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note that it discusses two distinct cases: an elderly weak person and a young man able to fast.
The passage first mentions the elderly weak then shifts to the young able.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For the elderly weak, not informing is not sinful because old age is a likely place for mercy. For the young able, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to not inform him.
The term 'makruh tahrimi' indicates it is close to haram but not proven by definitive evidence.
3
Grasp the legal reasoning (talil)
The reasoning for the elderly weak is that old age invites mercy, so omitting the information is excused. For the young able, the reasoning is based on al-Walwaliji's statement that it is obligatory to inform and disliked to leave it.
This shows how Hanafi jurists use 'mazinnah' (likely place) as a basis for rulings.
4
Understand the scope of the ruling
The author says the ruling is absolute, covering both obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) fasts.
This means the ruling applies whether the fast is mandatory or voluntary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى بمعصية، ولأن الشيخوخة مظنة المرحمة. وإن كان شاباً يقوى على الصوم يكره أن لا يخبره، والظاهر أنها تحريمية لأن الولوالجي قال : يلزمه أن يخبره ويكره تركه . أطلقه فشمل الفرض والنفل
Until [he does so] with disobedience, and because old age is a likely place for mercy. And if he is a young man able to fast, it is disliked that he does not inform him, and the apparent [view] is that it is prohibitively disliked because al-Walwaliji said: It is obligatory for him to inform him and it is disliked to leave it. He [the author] made it absolute, so it includes obligatory and supererogatory [fasts].
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanation. It discusses the obligation of informing a person who is about to start a fast if he is likely to be harmed. The text distinguishes between an elderly weak person and a young strong person. For the elderly, not informing is not sinful because old age invites mercy. For a young man able to fast, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) not to inform him, based on al-Walwaliji's statement that it is obligatory to inform and disliked to omit. The ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory fasts.

Key Terms
تحريمية (tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) — close to haram but not proven by definitive evidence.
مظنة (mazinnah): A place or characteristic that is likely to evoke something; here, old age is likely to evoke mercy.
الشيخوخة (al-shaykhukhah): Old age; in this context, it is the characteristic that makes one a likely object of mercy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a young man able to fast is not informed about the fast according to al-Walwaliji?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is makruh tahrimi to not inform him.
C) It is haram to not inform him.
D) It is mustahabb to inform him.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling on informing about fasting depends on the person's strength: it is not sinful to omit for the elderly weak, but it is prohibitively disliked for the young able.

Forgetful Intercourse While Fasting: Immediate Withdrawal vs. Deliberate Movement
Rules on forgetful intercourse during fasting and an analogy with conditional divorce/manumission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful intercourse during fasting and identify when kaffarah is required based on the presence of deliberate movement after remembering.

Core Idea
Forgetful intercourse does not break the fast if withdrawal is immediate; only qada is due unless deliberate movement continues.

This passage clarifies the rulings for a fasting person who forgetfully engages in intercourse. The key distinction is whether he withdraws immediately upon remembering or continues, and whether he moves himself deliberately after remembering. The ruling also has implications for conditional divorce and manumission through analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetful intercourse while fasting. The ruling varies based on what the person does after remembering.
Forgetfulness is a valid excuse in Hanafi law.
2
Distinguish immediate withdrawal vs. continued emission
If he withdraws immediately upon remembering, the fast remains valid. If he continues and emits, qada is required.
No kaffarah in the latter case unless additional conditions.
3
Note the condition for kaffarah
Kaffarah is required only if he moves himself deliberately after remembering before emission. Without movement, only qada.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
4
Examine the analogy with conditional divorce/manumission
The same principle applies: if a man inserts and utters a conditional pronouncement, then does not move, the condition is not triggered; if he moves, it is triggered.
Analogy (qiyas) shows that deliberate movement is the decisive factor.
5
Understand the Hanafi emphasis on deliberate movement
Movement after the occurrence of the prohibiting factor (dawn or condition) is what triggers the additional obligation (kaffarah or divorce).
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from schools that impose kaffarah automatically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو بدأ بالجماع ناسياً فتذكر أن نزع من ساعته لم يفطر، وإن دام على ذلك أنزل فعليه القضاء ثم قيل لا كفارة عليه وقيل هذا إذا لم يحرك نفسه بعد التذكر حتى أنزل فإن حرك نفسه بعده فعليه الكفارة كما لو نزع ثم أدخل ولو جامع عامداً قبل الفجر وطلع وجب النزع في الحال فإن حرك نفسه فهو على هذا نظير ما قالوا لو أولج ثم قال لها إن جامعتك فأنت طالق أو حرة إن نزع أو لم ينزع ولم يتحرك حتى أنزل لم تطلق ولا تعتق، وإن حرك نفسه طلقت وعتقت ويصير مراجعاً بالحركة الثانية ويجب للأمة العقر ولأحد عليهما. كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : رجل أصبح يوم الشك متلوماً ثم أكل ناسياً ثم ظهر أنه من رمضان ونوى صوماً ذكر في الفتاوى أنه لا يجوز. وفي البقالي : النسيان قبل النية كما بعدها وصححه في القنية . قيد بالناسي لأنه لو كان مخطئاً أو مكرهاً فعليه القضاء خلافاً للشافعي فإنه يعتبر بالناسي ولنا أنه لا يغلب وجوده وعذر النسيان غالب، ولأن النسيان من قبل من له الحق والإكراه من قبل غيره فيفترقان كالمقيد والمريض العاجز عن بالرأس في قضاء الصلاة حيث يقضي المقيد لا المريض. وأما حديث «رفع عن أمتي الخطأ» فهو من باب الاقتضاء وقد أريد الحكم الأخروي فلا حاجة إلى إرادة الدنيوي إذ . لا هو ذلك حتى الأداء عموم واحد. وفي السراج عن الواقعات: إن رأى فيه قوة أن يتم الصوم إلى الليل ذكره وإلا فلا. والمختار أنه يذكره، وظاهر كلامهم أنه لا فرق بين الفرض ولو قضاء أو كفارة والنفل في أنه يذكره أو لا
And if he began intercourse forgetfully, then remembered, if he withdraws immediately he does not break the fast; if he continues to the point of emission, then qada is upon him; then it is said no kaffarah on him; and it is said [that is] if he did not move himself after remembering until he emitted; but if he moved himself after remembering, then kaffarah is upon him, as if he withdrew and then inserted. And if he intentionally had intercourse before dawn and dawn rises, withdrawal is obligatory immediately; if he moves himself, then it is analogous to what they said: if he inserted and then said to her 'if I have intercourse with you, you are divorced or free' and he did not withdraw or did not move until he emitted, she is not divorced and not freed; but if he moved himself, she is divorced and freed, and he becomes a returnee by the second movement, and for the slave-girl there is the 'uqr, and for one of them [obligation] against him. So in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: A man became on the day of doubt a متلوم (one in doubt), then ate forgetfully, then it became clear that it was Ramadan, and he intended a fast. It is mentioned in the fatawa that it is not permissible. And in al-Baqqali: Forgetfulness before the intention is like after it, and he corrected it in al-Qunyah. It is restricted to the forgetful, because if he was mistaken or coerced, then qada is upon him, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he considers [the ruling] like the forgetful. And for us, that [mistake] does not occur predominantly, and the excuse of forgetfulness is dominant; and because forgetfulness is from the one who has the right, while coercion is from someone else, so they differ like the bound patient and the one unable to sleep on head in the qada of prayer: the bound patient prays, not the patient. As for the hadith 'My community is pardoned for error,' it is from the category of necessity, and the intended meaning is the hereafter, so there is no need to intend the worldly [ruling] because that is not one general application. In al-Siraj from al-Waqi'at: If he sees strength in him to complete the fast until night, he mentions it; otherwise no. The chosen view is that he mentions it; apparent from their words is that there is no difference between obligatory even if qada or expiation, and supererogatory, regarding mentioning it or not.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage combines several rulings and discussions. First, it details the case of a person who forgetfully begins intercourse while fasting: if he withdraws immediately upon remembering, the fast is not broken; if he continues and emits, only qada is required, not kaffarah, unless he deliberately moves himself after remembering, then kaffarah. Next, it analogizes the case of intentional intercourse before dawn with the rulings of conditional divorce/manumission. Then, it addresses the متلوم (one in doubt on the day of doubt) who eats forgetfully and later learns it was Ramadan: according to the fatawa, he may not fast that day, but al-Baqqali corrects that forgetfulness before intention is like after intention, i.e., it does not matter. The passage then explains why the ruling is restricted to forgetfulness: if he was mistaken (e.g., thought dawn had not yet come) or coerced, qada is required, unlike the Shafi'i view. The Hanafi reasoning is that mistake is rare and forgetfulness is a common excuse, and forgetfulness is from the person himself while coercion is from others, so they differ. The hadith about pardon for error is interpreted as referring to the afterlife, not worldly rulings. Finally, the passage discusses whether to inform the متلوم: if he seems strong enough to complete the fast, inform him; otherwise not. The chosen view is to inform him, regardless of whether the fast is obligatory or supererogatory.

Key Terms
عقر ('uqr): Compensation paid to a slave-girl for intercourse mistakenly (here due to movement after conditional pronouncement).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a fasting person who forgetfully begins intercourse, remembers, and then deliberately moves himself until emission?
A) The fast is valid, no penalty.
B) Qada only, no kaffarah.
C) Qada and kaffarah.
D) Kaffarah only, no qada.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful intercourse while fasting requires immediate withdrawal; only qada unless deliberate movement, then kaffarah.

The Mutalawwim on the Day of Doubt: Forgetful Eating and Informing Him
Rules on the mutalawwim (person in doubt) who eats forgetfully on the day of doubt and the ruling on informing him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a mutalawwim who eats forgetfully on the day of doubt and state the recommended action regarding informing him if he begins fasting.

Core Idea
Forgetful eating on the day of doubt invalidates the fast for a mutalawwim; forgetfulness before intention is excused.

This passage discusses a special case: a person who is unsure whether it is Ramadan and does not intend to fast (mutalawwim). If such a person eats forgetfully and later learns it was Ramadan, the initial fatawa say he may not fast that day. However, al-Baqqali corrects that forgetfulness before intention is like forgetfulness after intention, meaning it is excused. The passage also explains why the ruling differs for mistake or coercion, and whether to inform the mutalawwim if he is seen fasting.

Guided Path
1
Define the mutalawwim
A mutalawwim is a person who is in doubt about whether the day is Ramadan or not, and does not intend to fast.
The term is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the initial ruling
According to the fatawa, if a mutalawwim eats forgetfully and later learns it was Ramadan, it is not permissible for him to fast that day (i.e., the fast is invalid).
This is the default ruling.
3
Note al-Baqqali's correction
Al-Baqqali corrected that forgetfulness before the intention is like forgetfulness after; thus the fast may be considered valid.
This is the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar).
4
Understand the restriction to forgetfulness
The ruling that qada is not required applies only to forgetfulness. If the person was mistaken (e.g., thought dawn had not come) or coerced, qada is wajib.
Shafi'i equates mistake and coercion with forgetfulness; Hanafi distinguishes.
5
Examine the ruling on informing the mutalawwim
If a mutalawwim is seen fasting and seems capable of completing, inform him; otherwise do not. The chosen view is to inform him regardless of the type of fast (obligatory or nafl).
This is based on al-Siraj and al-Waqi'at.
